I have periodontal disease and have struggled for 40 years with flossing and picking, deep cleanings at the dentist office and even some gum surgery to try to maintain my gums and teeth.<br />Two years ago I bought the Airflosser at my dentists office on their recommendation. Since then my periodontal problem has all but gone away and I no longer use dental floss (which I hate). My gums no longer bleed and my hygienist of 20 years says my gums have never been better.<br />The battery stays charged for about 2 weeks of use (once daily) when traveling and the only problem I have had is broken stems and some leaking where the stem mounts to the base which I cured with a couple of wraps of plumbers teflon tape. Also sometimes a vacuum lock develops in the water tank which restricts the flow of water but a quick opening of the fill port fixes that.

Ok so i got the airfloss device from a dental hygienist i used to work with, she picked up a few extra at a dental convention. after watching videos on youtube, reading reviews here on amazon and also using it myself, i feel it would be helpful to say this... If you are already a faithful and diligent flosser, do not stop your flossing! This item is not as effective as daily flossing, but in a world where most people dont floss or dont floss correctly, this can be quite helpful, especially if used with a mouth rinse or flouridde in the evening before bed. The product works well at loosening plaque but can have some difficulty removing larger pieces of food. I suggest using this first with a mouthwash, then brushing. My mouth does feel cleaner and healthier, as a sporadic flosser this will improve my oral health, but it is not a substitute for flossing. One more word of advice, it takes a few days to learn not to spray your mirror, etc... (practice the first time with water, and always turn it off as soon as you take it out of your mouth to prevent accidental firing). also if you dont line it up correctly it may misfire (spray out of your mouth), or not fire. A correct firing will shoot through your teeth and to the middle of your mouth to your tongue, if you didnt get a good result, reposition it and refire until you do. after a week, you will know how to use it with your mouth, which teeth need different angles, etc... Good luck and enjoy!

  40. My gums tend to get nasty quickly, even with flossing/brushing on a regular basis, so I'm always on the look out for new gadgets to try to keep ahead of the gingivitis fight. I've never liked floss due to the tight gaps between some of my teeth, though the small handled flossers have been my choice for the past couple of years. I've tried water flossers, but they are just too messy and time consuming. So of course when I saw this, I jumped on the pre-order.<br /><br />The function is very simple - turn on, place the tip between your teeth, and fire away. For each push of the button, a burst of air and water blasts through your gumline. The water reservoir holds just a small amount of water, and is good for at least two full \\"flossings.\\" Learning where/how to position the tip for each tooth-gap is something you'll figure out in short time - if you don't have the tip in the right spot, you'll feel the air/water burst kind of \\"back up\\" in the tube, and basically \\"fizzle\\" out as it releases at the tip. With a little work, I'm able to find a good spot for all of my teeth to ensure a good blast of flossing.<br /><br />To test the effectiveness, I used the Airfloss after eating a good portion of steak, since particles of the steak tend to wedge tightly between my teeth. The Airfloss was able to dislodge the particles and clean out between my teeth pretty well, though some spots required more than one burst. Afterwards, I ran a handled flosser through my teeth to check, and there was very little leftover matter for the flosser to remove. I'd say the Airfloss was just as effective as the handled flosser, and easier to use since just a push or two of the button did the work. For regular morning/evening flossing, a single press is effective.<br /><br />I'll be interested to use this for a full period between professional cleanings, to see if there is any noticeable difference in my gum health from the Airfloss.<br /><br />**Update 8/27/2011**<br />I've found that I tend to follow the Airfloss tip with my tongue on the back-side of my teeth. This decreases effectiveness of the Airfloss, as it holds in any particulate that might get blown out the back of your teeth/gums. I've noticed much improved results when keeping my tongue away from where I'm using the Airfloss. A good \\"blast\\" from the Airfloss should be felt on the other side of your mouth.<br /><br />Pros:<br /><br />Easy to use.<br />Requires little water.<br />Very portable.<br />No need to stick your fingers in your mouth.<br />Not messy like a water flosser.<br /><br />Cons:<br /><br />Take a bit of experimentation to find optimal spots.<br />Will splatter the area/mirror if you don't close your mouth while using!e on the back-side of my teeth. This decreases effectiveness of the Airfloss, as it holds in any particulate that might get blown out the back of your teeth/gums. I've noticed much improved results when keeping my tongue away from where I'm using the Airfloss. A good \\"blast\\" from the Airfloss should be felt on the other side of your mouth.   67. If you play tennis, you may have several types of racquets. If you golf, you definitely have many types of clubs. When you exercise, you perform many types of exercises, routines, and use all sorts of equipment. Oral hygiene is similar, and therefore is best viewed from a fitness perspective. The Sonicare Airfloss is a new piece of Oral Fitness equipment. if you really think about it a moment, you will realize that regular flossing is almost like moving plaque from one tooth to another and jamming it into the gums. Yet it is standard advice to floss in this manner. Now here we have a unique piece of equipment that blasts junk out from between teeth and is easier and faster than flossing. Plus, you can add all sorts of medicaments into the reservoir for added effects. You can't very well do that with floss. A couple days ago, I purposely got a bunch of chicken jammed between my teeth. I tried flossing it out and all that happened was I crammed the chicken deeper between my teeth. I used the Airfloss, and after six blasts, the chicken flew out and hit my tongue. Most people don't floss. Many people can't floss. Only about 20% of us floss at all, and most of the time it's done incorrectly. We need innovations like this to help people obtain better oral health. I don't think it's valid comparing the Airfloss with other Oral Fitness products any more than comparing various exercise devices. They all have different uses, benefits, targets, etc. I think it's odd that people may have many types of sporting equipment, or tools, but when it comes to oral health, they may have only a toothbrush and very rarely floss. I think we should expand our oral health products to include all sorts of products for specific uses, just like we do with tools and sporting equipment. Therefore, I highly recommend the Sonicare Airfloss for that reason.

  111. The Airfloss could turn you into a drool monster, or Dracula. Or, it could just do a great job of cleaning between your teeth. I'm banking on the latter. (After nearly 2 years of use and some of the best checkups I've ever had, I am a true believer in this device, Jan. 10, 2013 update)<br /><br />I like this product. The gadget aspect of it is nice. The handle is about the diameter of two Sonicare toothbrushes, it's pretty big, but feels really good in my hand. My teeth felt like I had been to the dentist for a cleaning. The airfloss does power through built up food nicely. I didn't floss for a few days, and all the spices, little bits of food, and Wonder White bread stuck between my teeth came right out. I can reach to the back of my mouth really easily, those molars tend to never get a flossing, they will now.<br /><br />Update January 10, 2013: Sadness, the handle stopped working. I called Philips and they are sending me a brand new handle. Turns out this has a 2 year warranty for any defects. This is way beyond my expectations. The customer support person talked me through troubleshooting to be sure the handle was malfunctioning. Once he determined the unit was broken, I was on hold for a few minutes, and a brand new handle is on its way. Included in the replacement is a return shipping label. This is by far the best warranty service I have ever witnessed. He simply needed a serial number and there were absolutely no questions asked to replace it.<br /><br />Two dentist visits between my last update. The first was excellent, no gum bleeding, very healthy and my dentist was impressed. The most recent visit wasn't as good, I slacked off using the Airfloss and it showed. It is important for me to use this twice a day, and I was skipping days. Yes I got a stern talking to by my dentist and hygenist (I deserved it).<br /><br />People can debate that this is not a replacement for flossing. That's fine. But in my hands, this thing is so much better than flossing - I hate flossing. Yes I hate flossing more than anybody can imagine and I won't do it regularly. I use this thing twice a day and am happy using ing. Theory and practice are two very different things. Nearly two years of use proves that to me.<br /><br />December 1, 2011 Dentist Visit Update: This is one of the best dental appointments I have ever had. My experience with the Airfloss is outstanding. I started using this device the day of my last check up six months ago. I have used it religiously for the past 6 months, and today is the day I got the results of using this. There is absolutely no question about it, my mouth and teeth are much healthier than they have ever been. Normally my gums show some bleeding during the cleaning, and they are usually somewhat red. Today, they were healthy and pink, with very little bleeding. The hygienist normally spends a long time scraping my teeth, today she spent maybe half the time. Both my dentist and hygienist said the device works and are happy with how much better my gums and teeth look - they will begin recommending it to their patients. This is my personal experience with the Airfloss. I have a lot of trouble flossing or even remembering to floss (actually I pretty much hate flossing), I have no problem brushing my teeth twice a day. Adding this 15 second step to my routine, and I can get a great check up - I'm totally sold.<br /><br />August 26, 2011 Update: My teeth have never felt cleaner now that I use this at least daily, sometimes twice per day. As I said below, I travel with this I love it that much. A note for those of you that have closely spaced teeth. My wife has trouble finding floss that will fit between her teeth - this device does not work for her. I've never had trouble getting floss between my teeth, so I must be an ideal candidate. If you have very closely spaced teeth (you probably know if you do), you might want to pass on the Airfloss.<br /><br />July 12, 2012 Update: Some of the other reviews of this product and comments have complained that this is not ADA approved, and that water piks are their favorite thing to use because they are reliable. The ADA has never approved a water pik - they are not ADA approved. In fact no electric dental gadget has been approved by them. So the ADA mark is nice, but missing that approval does not mean a device is a bad device.<br /><br />The orginal review:<br /><br />I'm not a huge fan of the reservoir cover; it doesn't close with a snap that would reassure me it is closed. Not every single speck of food was removed in one pass. I can see that using this every day, between my teeth will be cleaner. Sometimes it's hard to get the little head lined up exactly right, either getting a shot of water in my mouth, on the mirror, or misfiring (the little tip was plugged by my teeth and nothing came out).<br /><br />My gums did bleed a little the first use, but they also do that when I don't floss for a few days. The bleeding stopped after the third day. I wasn't dripping blood from my mouth like Dracula; it was that redness right around the gum line.<br /><br />There is no ADA (American Dental Association) certificate on this device. That certificate would be nice. This is a very new product. It just happened that the day after I received this, I had a dentist appointment. My dentist is pretty aware of the latest teeth cleaning devices (he actually had a Sonicare toothbrush a good long while before they were available in the store), he had never heard of this. This isn't a dentist's approval of the Airfloss, but he did say it looked like a really good idea. And anything that would encourage people to floss more is a good thing.<br /><br />January 4, 2012 Update: A little clarification on the ADA - I visited their site and looked over what products have ADA seal of approval. Would it surprise you to know that not a single electric toothbrush, or water pic has their seal of approval? In fact nothing with an electric cord has their seal of approval. I have no experience with this organization, how they approve products, or their rules for what to accept for testing, but it appears to me this device, along with all the other electric dental products, will not get their seal of approval. Not because they are bad products, but because the ADA just doesn't do that, plain and simple.<br /><br />A lot of different people could use the Airfloss: People with big hands that find flossing the rear teeth difficult. People with a disability where a caregiver needs to floss for them, or have difficulty holding floss with two hands for themselves. Or people that want to be encouraged to floss more often.<br /><br />I have had a Philips Sonicare toothbrush for around three years. That toothbrush takes a lot of getting used to, getting over the crazy tickling on my teeth, avoid spraying toothpaste all over the room, and getting over the annoying noise.<br />Like the Sonicare toothbrush, the Airfloss takes some practice. My first few times around I managed to drool all over my shirt and completely wash down the bathroom mirror. Of course some of you will be more mechanically inclined and figure out how to avoid the drool bath and mirror cleaning. The secret is to hold your lower lip up, and make sure the little head is seated between your teeth and not on an angle. It's also important to hold the unit with the tip up.<br /><br />The device is incredibly simple. It is basically a liquid reservoir and a pump that fires a shot of water and air out the little tip. Pressing on the big green button at the top of the white handle, starts off a winding up noise, a deep click, and a puff. At the base there is a rubber sealed on / off switch. The charger looks like a small hockey puck. Like the Sonicare toothbrush, charging is by induction, meaning there are no electrical contacts.<br /><br />The liquid reservoir holds about a tablespoon and is supposed to be good for two uses. I actually have to refill mine for a lap around mymouth, maybe I have way more teeth than the average bear. The instructions allow for water or mouthwash in the reservoir. I like the idea of mouthwash; it feels really great in my mouth. Mouthwash can form a hard residue, and that could plug up the machine.<br /><br />It's hard to say if sharing this device is a good or bad idea. The tip is solid plastic and shiny, there are no bristles at all on it. A little rinse off with mouthwash should clean the tip off for somebody else to use. Well you know, for your significant other, not a community thing for strangers. The tip is really hard to remove, I wouldn't want to constantly snap it off and snap on another tip.<br /><br />Philips recommends changing the tip every six months. Hard for me to see exactly what could go wrong with the tip. But they are really inexpensive (around nine dollars for a pair [[ASIN:B0052JNCFE Philips Sonicare HX8002/60 Airfloss Replacement NOuncezles, 2 Count]]).<br /><br />One charge is supposed to last about two weeks. The unit is fully charged overnight.<br /><br />The instruction manual is very nice. They even include instructions on how to dispose of the unit when it has expired and you no longer need it. About four times they repeat that this procedure will destroy the unit. The pictures are to wrap the unit in a cloth, smash it with a hammer, and remove the battery. The smashed bits can be tossed in the trash, and the battery should be recycled. This is a new one for me; I've never seen a company that recommends smashing their device with a hammer to remove the battery. Pretty cool Philips.<br /><br />This is a million times better than a water pik. The Airfloss is a puff between the teeth, a water pik is like a squirt gun all over the place. And there's that nasty hose with the water pik.<br /><br />I'm so guilty of not flossing, and know I should floss more often. During one six month period, I flossed every night and used mouthwash, that dentist appointment was quick and easy - almost no scraping necessary. The rest of the time, my dentist reminds me to floss more. This gadget just might get me to floss every night now.approval. I'm getting the swing of it. If you don't get the spray right, it doesn't clean well. 3. It's not quite as neat as I would have liked. I get a bit of dribble, but no where near the mess of a waterpik. 4. Works well with both mouth rinse and water. Whether shooting the stuff between your teeth has more benefit than just rinsing your mouth when done, I don't know. Overall, I like it. I will continue using it. After 1 week I see a difference in my teeth. They look and feel much cleaner. I see huge potential benefits for people who do not floss or are sporadic flossers like me. If you are a habitual flosser now, you are probably already getting a better cleaning than this gadget will give you. I'm giving it 3 stars because I think it performed well, but not as well as advertised. I add another review after I've been using it a while longer.   203. First of all, I must disclose that I work in the Healthcare/ Dental industry. I encounter a lot people everyday who need to floss more or wish flossing was easier, including myself. It should be noted that this is not a form of advice in any way or matter, the opinions here are just my personal thoughts on the device.<br /><br />Gums, bleeding and Flossing<br />gums bleed if bacteria grows in the form of plaque on your teeth. Bacteria uses calcium from you saliva to form plaque. Plaque/Calculus form on all surfaces of the teeth and is easily removed by brushing. The problem is with plaque that forms under the gum and in between the teeth. Your body tries to kill the bacteria by pumping more blood to the gums to fight it (inflammation) and thus gums bleed.<br />Compared to other oral irrigation devices:<br />I have used the Waterpik for a couple of years and was a little skeptical when I first used the Sonicare. As apposed to the Waterpik, the Sonicare air flosser uses interrupted air/water mist to clean between the teeth. Waterpik uses a continuous jet stream. I was skeptical because the reservoir in the waterpik is 210ml and the air flosser holds about a table spoon full. More about that later.<br />How it works:<br />The concept is that if you push water hard enough through the spaces between teeth the water stream will carry with it any food or debris that are stuck there and thus less food for the bacteria to grow on. There is a major difference between that and brushing/flossing. When you floss or brush, you interrupt the formation of plaque. So no the air flosser will not remove plaque. Here is where the air flosser will work, the more food you have between your teeth, the more resources the bacteria will have to form plaque and calculus. by using the air flosser you slow down this process.<br />How to use:<br />I use a mouth wash to fill it up instead of water in the hope that some of that will be retained between my teeth and kill bacteria that is growing there.<br />you take the tip and fit it interproximally between 2 teeth from the outside (labial: lip side) and activate, move to the next 2 teeth and repeat until you do the whole mouth. I activate the water jet twice for every space from the lip side and once from the tongue side (lingual). sonicare does not recommend this because they are afraid that you might over do it and damage your gums. I dont advocate it either so do at your own risk. I just dont feel one pump will remove everything. Now this is a problem for me because I find I have to fill up the reservoir 2 or 3 times to do the whole mouth.<br />Many people complain that it makes a mess, but with time it will become easy, just keep your mouth closed.<br />Who is it and is it not for:<br />If you use floss and do it regularly then this is not for you. what you are doing is way better habit.<br />If you have tight contacts, you know because when you eat meat nothing sticks between your teeth, this is not for you.<br />Now if you have wide contacts, and you know because you cant eat a taco without reaching for anything to clean between your teeth, then this is for you.<br />If you tried flossing and you really cant get yourself to do it no matter what, then this is for you and way better than nothing.<br />If your gums bleed every time you brush or floss then pushing some of that mouthwash in there might actually help by reducing the number of bacteria and the food available for it to grow.<br />When you go to your dentist and get a deep cleaning, the dentist uses a sonic instrument to disrupt the plaque and to break it down. This is ultimately what you need if your gums bleed. once the plaque is gone and you floss/brush/air floss, the formation of plaque is inhibited and your gums live happy, bacteria free.

  206. I recently started caring about my dental health after part of my tooth fell out because it was undermined by a huge cavity. I can say with confidence that for the past decade or so, I wouldn't brush more than three times a month, and that was on a good month, and I practically never flossed. After the incident with the tooth, I became concerned with my dental health and hygiene and started looking up what I could do to start fixing up my teeth. Everything pointed me towards Philips Sonicare as the brand to go to for dental health equipment. I first purchased a [[ASIN:B0052JN7XG Philips Sonicare HX9332/05 DiamondClean Rechargeable Electric Toothbrush]] to brush my teeth with after looking at numerous reviews for this and other alternatives online, and the next day I followed up with this Sonicare Airfloss to complete the package.<br /><br />Upon getting it, the first thing you notice is the kind of odd shape and size of the tool, though it isn't at all unwieldy or ugly. It's sleek like all other Sonicare products and looks beautiful on my counter next to the DiamondClean. I got some [[ASIN:B005BUNTTS Crest Pro-Health Rinse Complte Fresh Mint 1 lt.]] mouthwash to use as the liquid agent for this utensil. Basically what the Airfloss does is when you turn it on and press the activate button, it will shoot out a very high pressure burst of air full of tiny micro-droplets of water or mouthwash, whichever you prefer to use (I used mouthwash) that literally blasts out all the food particulates and plaque and other gunk that gets stuck between your teeth and gums. I advise using a mouthwash instead of water for this because the mouthwash contains other ingredients to neutralize bacteria and destroy and prevent plaque regrowth and other sterilizing stuff.<br /><br />To use the Airfloss the first time, first make sure that you put it on the charger and let it charge fully for 24 hours. This will condition the battery and make sure that it will last you its full lifespan and capacity, which is enough to last over two weeks if you use it twice a day. After charging it for the first time, you flip up the clear cap of the reservoir on the back of the unit and fill it up with about two tablespoons or teaspoons (I forget) of water, mouthwash, or other cleaning agent of choice. Then press the power button near the bottom of the unit so the little green LED light turns on, then point the nozzle away from you (or wherever, it doesn't matter right now) and press the activate button a few times, which will prime the unit and bring the liquid you added to it into the system. I find that you shouldn't press the activate button more than once per second because if you do it too fast, the motor will kind of backfire because it will try to suck in air and burst out the stuff before the previous burst has fully left the nozzle. So, the first few burst the first time you use the Airfloss will be just air but after that, it will shoot out very high pressure air and mouthwash or water.<br /><br />Now for the real regular use, you try to hold the device so that the little outlet of the nozzle is perpendicular against the surface of your teeth and is resting in between your teeth, while the rubber face surrounding the nozzle outlet is gently resting against the surface of your teeth. Then press the activate button and *Puft!* you're good to go. Repeat for all your teeth including your rear molars. It will take a few uses to perfect the form and style in which you use the Airfloss, so the first time, you might find that some of the burst sprays out and dirties up your mirror or wall, but you'll get the hang of it soon enough. Ideally, you should be able to eventually stick the nozzle in your mouth and know where to place it by muscle memory or feel and keep your lips closed around the neck of the nozzle so that nothing sprays out of your mouth, which can happen because the burst is so fast and high pressured that it can bounce off your tongue or your teeth ifyou don't place it properly.<br /><br />I find this device to be a much better alternative to manual flossing with string because manually flossing doesn't always remove all the gunk between your teeth whereas the Airfloss does, flossing with string can cut up your gums which allows more evil bacteria to penetrate deeper into your gums and can cause problems. Manual flossing can also result in small fibers of broken off floss string getting stuck between your teeth and making a mess, and finally, unless you use a very liberal amount of string floss, you're just moving the bacteria and plaque from one tooth to the next because all the stuff that comes out from between your teeth gets stuck on the floss string, and then you take that same (now dirty) string and stick it between your next teeth. The Airfloss avoids all these problems and I feel that it blasts and cleans out between your teeth and gums more effectively than string floss would even if it didn't have these issues.<br /><br />Now let's talk about results. I've been using the Airfloss 2-3 times per day for just over a month in conjunction with my Sonicare DiamondClean toothbrush and new, better brushing habits. I have no plaque at all on or between my teeth, and my gums feel refreshed and my teeth and mouth feel clean after using the Airfloss with the mouthwash I add to it. Since I started using these products a month ago, my teeth have whitened over 5 shades whiter, which is a night-and-day difference and I've actually received compliments and surprise when people see my new teeth and the way they sparkle now. I've even let some other family members use the Airfloss with spare nozzles and they all say that after using it, their mouth feels the cleanest it has ever felt. If oral hygiene and dental health are concerns of yours, and even if they aren't, this is a great product that will definitely enhance and better your life.

It is nowhere near effective as regular flossing using traditional dental floss, waxed or unwaxed, thin or thick, in removing food particles between teeth. My teeth are straight without any missing teeth and have no severe crowding or tight contacts between any teeth. Therefore, tight contacts and crowding was not an issue when I was evaluating this product. The main problem is that the water/air pulse generated by this device is simply insufficient to completely and in some cases even partially dislodge the debris. I end up having to repeatedly blast the same area to no avail. Furthermore, I have to refill this device 6-7 times before I'm finished, which I find tedious and more time-consuming than traditional flossing. I usually end up having to reach for a floss afterwards.<br /><br />As an adjunct device to supplement flossing, this device might be marginally useful for older patients with large gaps between their teeth. Even then, there are better options such as interdental/interproximal brushes and Waterpik devices. For patient with braces, where food particles on the brackets are more of an issue than in-between areas, this device might be useful. However, Waterpik is still a better option here as well.<br /><br />Philips brochure for efficacy of this product is overly optimistic, like a lot of marketing stuff in general. Save your money.   226. This is my first review and I felt compelled to put my thoughts out into the Amazon ether because so many people seem to think this product doesn't work and I want to try and right the ship as best I can for those who already own one as well as for those who are considering making the investment.<br /><br />First off, I've owned this product for 9 months and to me, it works. I've been to the dentist once during this 9 month period and they noticed a distinct difference in the amount my gums bleed and believe me, they used to bleed. Leading up to that appointment, I only used the Airfloss and I wasn't even using it on a daily basis - maybe a few times a week (I have consistency issues, hence why I purchased this product to begin with - I hated flossing).<br /><br />The crux of the issue with this product to many, in my opinion, is that people aren't using it properly. It seems most people expect to be able to fit the nozzle in between your teeth but I don't think that's the intent of the product at all. The purpose is to position the nozzle such that the jet of water is aimed directly at the bottom of the piece of gum that sits between your teeth so that the microfilm that builds up there can be washed away. This doesn't require the nozzle to be pushed in between your teeth or pushed hard into your gums - it just needs to be aimed at the right spot, that's all.<br /><br />The way I use it (and I believe it works great this way) is as follows: I rest the nozzle very lightly against my teeth, sometimes not even at all, and make sure it's aimed at the bottom of the piece of gum that falls between my teeth. If you aim it higher, the water's just going to ricochet off your gums and splash your mirror. Why? Because there's no space there for the water to move through and clean anything. The purpose is to allow the water to get around the gum and to do that, you must aim towards the bottom of the gum, where there's space. Again, no need to get the nozzle in betweenyour teeth or pressed very firmly up against your gum. Give it a touch of space and once you press the button, the jolt should cause the nozzle to lightly tap your teeth and you should be good to go. And don't aim the Airfloss upwards - the water needs to be able to escape out the back, so keep it level. Think of it as if you're trying to hose down someone covered in mud - you wouldn't walk right up to the person and slam the nozzle directly into their stomach and then pull the lever, right?<br /><br />Yes, you need to practice a few times to get it right but once you get the process down, you can floss while walking around your house with no issues. It's much quicker than normal flossing in my opinion as well - I usually give each gap a couple presses and I'm still done in a minute.<br /><br />Overall, I think the product works as advertised and I continue to use this on a regular basis. It just takes a little bit of tweaking/practice but I think it can work for everyone, regardless of mouth/gum size.

  385. The Philips Sonicare Airfloss takes a little practice and a little getting used to, but surprisingly, it's worth the effort.<br /><br />It's an easy to use little machine - plug in the charger and let it power up for 24 hours, fill the reservoir with water, prime the pump with a few button presses, and you're off to the races. Usually a single button press between each tooth does the trick, a quick shot of air and water that blasts out smaller food particles pretty well. I can feel it working, cleaning as I work my way around, and it only takes a minute or two to be done. Bonus points for no nasty floss to throw away.<br /><br />It's reasonably attractive and doesn't take up much room either. The charging stand supports the Airfloss in an upright position, so you can stash it in a corner of your counter and barely notice its there until you need it. It doesn't look like a Big Scary Dental Device - nice to have something not terribly intimidating.<br /><br />It is a little on the messy side, though, especially the first few times you use it. If you don't place the head just right, it's almost inevitable that you'll get some spray reflected onto the bathroom mirror (or whatever or whoever happens to be in front of you). With practice, this gets better over time, but have a paper towel ready for those first few go-rounds. Also something to watch for the first few times: blood. Particularly if you're like me and weren't very good about flossing previously, you'll likely see some bleeding the first few times you use the Airfloss. If you keep doing it, that goes away (which is a good sign your gums are healthier too).<br /><br />Finally, if there's something big really stuck between your teeth, you may still need the old-school waxed floss now and again - the Airfloss doesn't get everything, but it gets most of the noticeable stuff.<br /><br />I honestly didn't expect to like the Airfloss much, but I can already see that as long as I don't mind a little extra water to clean up, I floss a lot more often with this than I ever did with string floss. Color me pleasantly surprised... and doing a better job of keeping my teeth clean.ean up, I floss a lot more often with this than I ever did with string floss. Color me pleasantly surprised... and doing a better job of keeping my teeth clean.

  416. Sharp bursts of air and water leaves a clean feel in the mouth. However, I would be extremely skeptical about the claim that it is a replacement for flossing. A lot of mouthwashes and water jet devices have made such claims to the chagrin of dental and health professionals. There is no replacement for regular (ideally twice daily) flossing. Period. I would describe this device as a less cumbersome variation of the water pic. Such devices can be especially helpful for those with braces. But the science was long settled that they do not replace flossing. However, they do have a role as adjuncts to brushing and flossing. The word \\"Airfloss\\" is an outcome of a marketing department, not peer reviewed research. Flossing perturbs newly formed plaque well below the gum line. This device offers no pathway to possibly replicate that. What \\"Airfloss\\" can do is target some of the plaque on recessed surfaces missed by flossing/brushing due to tooth curvature. To sum up the Airfloss does have a role in dental hygiene. Just don't fall for the marketing BS.You can bet your socks ADA will not be endorsing floss replacement claims at any time. If you don't floss often, the solution is to change your habit and start doing it. Periodontal gum disease isn't just about your mouth. It has a bearing on heart attacks/strokes/diabetes and host of inflammatory factors in your blood. (I am a health professional).
